<Rate>3< /Rate>< Text>
Update:

I felt the need to update my review of La Sierra University due to the amount of attention that my original review attained and in order to further clarify certain aspects of my original review.

As a Military Veteran I attended LSU utilizing my GI Bill. At the time of my attendance the campus did not offer a dedicated team or staff member that could tend to the unique requirements of Veterans and requests from the Department of Veterans Affairs in a timely manner. There were many occasions in which I would have to call and remind the representative in charge of the program at that time to certify my attendance at the university in order to receive my financial aid from the VA. On at least one occasion there was a significant lapse in aid as the representative failed to certify my attendance for a significant amount of time. I had to reach out the VA directly and request a financial hardship payment in order to keep up with my bills I had at the time since I had no other form of income during my time as a student there.

Other campuses that I had attended prior to LSU always had a dedicated team of experts to assist Veterans on their higher education journey, even including small community colleges. I did not understand why a university of this size did not have something similar.

Some of the buildings on campus were brand new, including the equipment, and conference halls. Though on the other hand other buildings on campus were rapidly deteriorating to include the very desks and chairs students sat in everyday. On occasion when a student brought this up to a staff member or professor it was explained that although the university does generate a significant income from student's tuition the profits have to be distributed to other sister schools and programs within the organization.

Although the university offered great opportunities for students by providing jobs for them, to include opportunities for recent graduates. Some of the positions these recent graduates filled were counselors and tutors. Thought it is a great idea it failed to address key issues such as being able to reach someone with the proper knowledge of programs, available financial aid, and the ability to approve or deny eligibility for said programs. Being that most of the staff was comprised of student workers there was almost always a bottleneck in order to retrieve correct information or approvals.

You will also be required to attend service at least once a week if you commute to campus. If you are in the dorms I have heard it is up to at least 3 times a week, but I cannot confirm that as I did not live on campus. You need to keep this in mind as this was mandatory and I had plan accordingly. Though it was mandatory not everyone that attended respected the service or even seemed the least bit interested. Often people were sprawled out on the benches taking a nap, talking to one another, or playing on their cellphones and portable video game consoles.

As I understood Loma Linda University is a sister school of LSU so many of the students attending LSU were simply doing so in order to find an easier application path to Loma Linda. Things may have changed since my time there but this was the overall goal of many of my peers.

Ultimately I ended up withdrawing from LSU for the reasons mentioned above as well as others not mentioned. I do not know how significantly things have changed since my attendance but if you're planning on attending this institution I would highly suggest you do your own research and talk to current students on their opinions, especially if you are going to be utilizing your VA benefits to do so.<//Text>

< text>
I had plan to go to the fall but the google maps took me here. Very nice view and moderate trail. Because i was looking for a way to go toward the fall I lost the miles that I hiked. There were limited parking spots between ten to 15 cars. It should be easy for kids older than 8 and intresting. If you continue walking on mine path you will go to the beautiful part with running water under the shade of trees.</text>

<review>The Peking Duck was a work of art. Expertly prepared, moist and generous!! Probably the nicest people you'd ever run into who clearly love what they do, and it comes through in their food!! <Review>We picked up our car at the Los Angeles Airport and drove up to Eureka. We spent the night in Eureka and when we woke up the 2019 GMC Acadia that we were given in LA was having a serious malfunction. When we started the vehicle all the lights on the dash come on and we had multiple error messages pop up on the screen stating "Occupant Restraint Error," "ABS Error" etc. and none of the signals, speedometer, fuel gauge or radio controls would work. We tried to call roadside assistance but was hung up on after explaining our problem to the representative on the phone. So, we checked on our phones and realized there was a Hertz rental location less than a mile away and we decided to drive over.
Upon arriving at the Hertz location in Eureka we felt relieved because there were multiple vehicles (Several Grand Caravans and a couple of Tahoes) on the lot so we figured they would be able to easily switch us into another vehicle. Boy where we wrong! After speaking with the young man at the counter he explained that he did not know what they were going to do because all the vehicles on the lot were reserved for pickups later that day but he thought they had a Chevy Equinox that we could take. After looking at the Equinox we determined that it was much too small for use considering we had 3 adults and a toddler in a chair seat along with all our luggage and also considering that we had reserved a Standard SUV Group L SFAR (Grand Cherokee or Similar) we felt this was a considerable downgrade. We were then told that they could have us ride over to the Eureka Airport location and if they had a vehicle more in the class that we needed. This seemed absurd so we asked if they could look and see what they had or even call over and check for us. We were then told that they had just had a plane land and was busy so they could not call over and ask for us. (Again, this was absolutely absurd and not our problem in the least). While we were still trying to figure it all out a GMC Terrain pulled into the lot to be returned. They ended up giving us the Terrain which we settled for because it was a little bigger than the Equinox. Nevertheless, we were still really cramped in the Terrain while previously we had plenty of room and was extremely satisfied with the Acadia that we originally had. We also were not offered a discounted rate because the vehicle we got stuck with would have actually been cheaper if we had rented that class.
Then to make matters much worse we were told that if they gas was below where it was when we picked it up that we would be charged $9.99 per gallon. I asked how we were supposed to know how much fuel was in the vehicle since the fuel gauge did not work and why they couldn‚Äôt wave that policy due to the circumstance and the agent just shrugged he did not know.
Why could they have not called the location at the airport for us? Why could they not have given us one of the vehicles on the lot that met our needs? Why couldn‚Äôt they have given us a car and gotten one from the airport or another nearby location for the pickup later in the day? We were already extremely inconvenienced by the situation and they were not trying to help us. We are repeat customers that had already paid for our rental and it actually seemed that they were trying to be as difficult as possible.

< text>
I'm a Hertz Gold Member and reserved my car online. When I went to pick it up, I was not given any explanation of charges, verbally or even a printed out receipt. I was unknowingly given a more expensive car than I had reserved, and charged $25 extra per day for it, again, not told to me when I picked up the car. When the car was returned, the guy at the desk, Jake, basically said there was nothing he could do about it, and to call Hertz if we wanted to. I called the Billing dept at Hertz and got yelled at by  the lady I spoke to, who told me to "take responsibility for this." I stayed courteous throughout the whole call because I really want to give her the benefit of the doubt that she's not a mean person; I really hope Hertz records their phone conversations. She then gave me the number for the Hertz location where I picked up the car and told me to talk to the manager, and when I called, it turns out that particular manager hasn't worked for Hertz for years. I had to call for three consecutive days, leaving a message & callback number every time (no one ever called me back), until a manager finally picked up the phone. The manager, Jessie, said she believed Jake when he said he gave me a verbal explanation of charges, even though she did confirm with him that I was never presented with a paper printout of the charges when I picked up the keys. She decided not to believe me, and I got the feeling that even if she did believe me, she wouldn't have done anything about it.< /text>
